style=\"letter-spacing: 0.05pt;\">h</span>e<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.05pt;\"> </span>origin<span style=\"letter-spacing: 0.1pt;\">a</span>l<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.35pt;\"> </span>B/Ls.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bill of Lading is the right to possession of cargo \u2014not ownership.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Cargo must be delivered to the consignee in the same condition as it was loaded. The description of cargo in the bill of lading is evidence in a court of law of the load port condition. If you find that there is a discrepancy between the B/L and actual condition the B/L must be claused with the appropriate wording to indicate the correct condition of the cargo. Often a prospective buyer decides to purchase the cargo on the basis of the B/L description. The cargo must then be delivered to the consignee at the discharge port in the condition described in the B/L or the cargo owner will claim compensation from the ship. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Bill of Lading is the most important of all cargo documents, and it represents a large amount of money . The Owner can be ruined by a Master who signs bills of lading in a mindless fashion.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The number of original B/L will appear on the B/L in a statement. The disport details on the B/L must be the same as intended in the charter party, otherwise master must refuse to sign.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The master must not sign anymore B/L in number than mentioned on the B/L unless these additional B/L are non negotiable. The number of original B/L is mentioned on the face of the B/L and master must ensure it is filled before signing that many originals only.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">A signed non negotiable B/L is as good as a photostat. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">When Bill of Lading originals are signed, the Mates receipts must be surrendered to master. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">It should be correctly dated for the time when the parcel completed loading which is the date of actual shipment. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The master unless instructed by the owners/ charterer should not sign B/L for a port of destination which his ship is physically incapable of reaching in safety. Check for NAABSA clause in South American river ports.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Freight if prepay able must be paid before master signs B/L--&nbsp; or there is no lien on cargo to recover the unpaid freight. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">This is also the time to get the Dead freight statement signed in return. Remember the Dead freight claim is not a discrepancy claim. For MOLOO if shore stops and ship could have taken more as per NOR declaration then issue a protest as well as a Dead freight statement. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The carrier will be unable to avoid liabilities which arise as a result of a failure to check the cargo unless a check is not reasonably possible. Furthermore, endorsements on the Bill of Lading, such as \"shipper's figures\", \"figures as per shore tally\", \"quantity and condition unknown\", or \"said to be ....\", will seldom absolve the carrier of blame if the Master has failed to check the particulars of the cargo to his own satisfaction.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Master should not state anything in the Bill of Lading which he believes to be inaccurate. If the Master finds errors or inaccurate information in the bill of lading he should correct it with an appropriate clause before signing it. If in doubt contact the Office.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Several Different shippers can load same cargo for several different consignees\u2014such cargoes must be covered by separate sets of B/L even if commingled.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Bill of Lading is a negotiable document, the cargo may be sold while en route, and the only evidence the buyer has of the nature, the quality and the quantity of the cargo is the <st1:personname w:st=\"on\">info</st1:personname>rmation given in the Bill of Lading. The Master is of course not expected to be an expert on each of the hundreds of chemicals&nbsp; that may be shipped.&nbsp; But he is not expected to throw his commonsense and judgement into the winds.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sampling procedures must be rigidly followed. In the chemical parcel tanker context it is cheaper to fail a wall wash than a tank first foot sample ( especially an unauthorised Texas foot ) and it is cheaper to fail a first foot than a disport out turn sample \u2013by say Benzene released by epoxy paint during voyage into Styrene Monomer<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Read charterers Blue book for instruction regarding cargo discrepancy. It will specify the percentage discrepancy to :---<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">1) Ignore ( usually up to 0.1% ) <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">2) To issue written LOP ( 0.1 to 0.5%) <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">3) Remeasure ,inform charterers and call P&amp;I. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Courts in many countries rule that the ship is not liable for shortages up to 0.5% &nbsp;( read the C/P )<o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Call P&amp;I club surveyor also in case of injury to crew, pollution , cargo contamination like first foot failure.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Obviously if something is too&nbsp; great for master to handle prior departure ( at an odd hour in a odd place ) refuse to sign B/L and pass it on to agent with proper letter of authority instructions. It is better to protest even if the cargo discrepancy ( ships figure less ) is just one ton.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the shore figure is not available prior sailing,&nbsp; Master must leave a short loading protest with the agent. The LOP must be prepared leaving the Bill of Lading figure blank.&nbsp; Instruct the agent to present it to the shipper on Master\u2019s behalf, once the Bill of Lading figure is declared.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the Shore Bill of Lading figures are not are not available before sailing from load port the Master must authorise the agent to sign the Bills of Lading on his behalf by means of a LOA for each grade.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If damaged cargo is loaded but not described as such in the Bill of Lading, the consignee has every right to assume that the damage has been caused by the ship and so her Owners will be held responsible.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Commingling</span></i><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">----If the shipper refuses the Master to clause the Bills of Lading with commingling statement then the Master should issue LOP and contact then operator. It is not uncommon for one cargo or parcel to be sold to various consignees, each of which receives a portion of the total quantity loaded.&nbsp; In these cases, the total quantity of all the Bills of Lading issued must equal the total loaded, and each Bill of Lading Bust contain the following commingling clause:<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">\"THIS SHIPMENT AS LOADED ON BOARD THE VESSEL AS PART OF ONE ORIGINAL LOT OF _________________ METRIC TONS WITH NO SEGREGATION AS TO PARCELS. NEITHER THE VESSEL NOR THE OWNERS ASSUME ANY RESPONSIBILITIES FOR THE CONSEQUENCES OF SUCH COMMINGLING NOR THE SEPARATION THEREOF AT THE TIME OF DELIVERY\"<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Bill of Lading must always be handed to the agent repeat the agent and definitely not the shipper. The master must recognise faces around him when he signs the bill of lading. The agent will hold on to the document unless he is authorized to release it by the Operator.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">When it is necessary to clause a B/L it is necessary to involve the assistance of a pro-active local cargo surveyor appointed by P&amp;I. For example if you are loading high Brix Molasses from a barge in Central America and you find that the cargo is heated to 60 deg C. Such high heating destroys the entire consignment due to thermal decomposition.---or the barge has been doing live steaming for its own convenience and foaming which is a visual effect of fermentation is readily apparent.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">B/L must&nbsp; be in the proper format as per the charter party. The number of originals and freight clauses must be in conformity with the terms and conditions of the charter party.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The format must include <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\">Paramount clause</b> <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\">incorporating Hague rules</b>. The letter of authorization to agent to sign B/L on master\u2019s behalf should specify that Paramount clause, New Jason's clause and York Antwerp rules clause must be incorporated.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Hague rules regulate all the rules relating to B/L. The Hague rules provide that \u201c no carrier shall be bound to state in Bill Of Lading any marks, numbers, quantity or weight which he has reasonable grounds of suspecting do not accurately represent the goods actually received or which he has no reasonable means of checking\u201d&nbsp;&nbsp; any terms in B/L which is inconsistent with Hague rules is automatically null and void. Deviation to save property ( not life ) is not an infringement of contact of carriage as per the Hague rules. They do not apply to deck cargo. Time for carrier to file recovery claims is extended. Servants of the carrier are afforded Himalaya protection. \u2013same rights and immunities as the carrier himself. There are special regulations for special cargoes\u2014normally time bar for cargo claims is one year. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">New Jason\u2019s clause provides&nbsp; that shippers/ consignee/ owners of cargo must contribute to general average whether it is carriers negligence or not. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">York Antwerp rules provide that general average and salvage are payable according to this. Expenses for delay at port of refuge, wages and subsistence for crew are covered. General average continues even is adventure is no longer in peril.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The master must NOT accept a letter of Indemnity to issue a clean B/L for bad cargo as courts have regarded that this practice as a collusion between the shipper and the carrier to defraud the consignee. Master is fully responsible for the cargo condition and LOI will not be honoured if things go wrong. In some circumstances with a valued and trusted customer the owner may tell the Master to accept LOI.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The cargo description in the Bill of Lading is based on the Mate\u2019s receipt; therefore the Mate\u2019s receipt should be treated as respectfully as the Bill of Lading. The master must be directly involved with Mates receipts. If the Mate without guidance has ignored basic caution it affects the endorsements on the Bill of Lading.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A Mate\u2019s receipt must not be signed if it contains any conditions which are contradictory to the Charter Party. The Mates Receipt cannot contain blanket appraisals like cargo has been \u2018stowed to Master\u2019s satisfaction\u2019 .If such clauses appear, the Mate must delete these before signing. The Mate\u2019s receipt is just a cargo receipt .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In case of mail delay and original B/L does not reach disport in time the cargo can be discharged under a LOI against bank guarantee made in a proper format . One of the formats is with bank guarantee and the other one is without bank guarantee when owner says guarantee is not required. Both formats are available in the P&amp;I club rule book--which states under which country law disputes will be settled . This LOI must come from Head Charterer to Head Owner and not from some local shipper to some Sub Charterer. So do not discharge unless advise has been received from Head Owners that \u2018indemnity\u2019 has been obtained.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Only the Master or someone expressly authorised by the Master in writing can sign the Bill of Lading.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If Master authorises agent to sign B/L , the LOA must contain the words\u201d in accordance with the Mate\u2019s receipts\u201d<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the vessel is on time-charter the Master should not issue any LOA without prior approval from head charterers.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The vessel is required to unberth as soon as possible upon completion and in such circumstances the Bill of Lading must be given to agents to sign and release them when instructed by the Operator.&nbsp; The LOA for agent to sign B/L must be signed and stamped by the agent.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The agent must also be instructed to scan and email the Bill of Lading to Operator for approval.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Express B/L: NIL original B/L, only non negotiable straight or \u201c express\u201d B/L . This is only when receiver and shipper is same company. Say UCC to UCC or DOW to DOW. It contains clause \u201c Express B/L : cargo to be delivered / released to consignee without production of original B/L\u201d.&nbsp; It states \u201c No or zero originals \u201c. Here consignee at disport need not produce Bill of Lading. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">A clean B/L is often the requirement of a bank if the holder of the B/L requires payment under a letter of credit. In many cases the shipper will insist or implore that they need a \u2018clean' Bill of Lading\u2019 in order to release the bank payment under a letter of credit. The Master must remain strong and <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\">NEVER </b>&nbsp;agree to sign a \u2018clean\u2019 Bill of Lading for damaged or contaminated chemicals no matter how much pressure is put on him by the shipper or his stooges.&nbsp; The Master must seek help by contacting the responsible operator who will then decide what should be done, e.g. calling in an independent surveyor to inspect the cargo etc.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Some charter parties contain a clause to the effect that \u2018Master is to sign Bill of Lading as presented\u2019.&nbsp; This does not give the shipper the right to demand a \u2018clean\u2019 Bill of Lading for \u2018unclean\u2019 cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Always remember that the Master does not only have a right but also a duty to clause the Bill of Lading in case of cargo defects, since the clausing is meant to protect the Owner as well as the consignee.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; The Master should always make sure that the Bill of Lading is marked: -\u2018Freight payable as per charter party.\u2019<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The shipper sometimes request \u2018Freight collect\u2019 to be inserted on the Bill of Lading. \u2018Freight collect\u2019<b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"> </b>means that the freight is payable upon delivery and the Master must therefore not sign the Bill of Lading unless Operator has authorised to do so.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Charterers might hold back the freight until the cargo has been delivered even if the contrary has been agreed to in the charter party.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">At the discharge port the master must only deliver the cargo to a bonafide holder of an original B/L\u2014usually there are three originals.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the B/L is OPEN then he can deliver the cargo to who ever presents one of the three originals (the bearer) provided he has no reason to suspect fraud. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the B/L is STRAIGHT he should check that the party claiming delivery (consignee )is the same as named on the document. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the B/L is NEGOTIABLE the master must check if the document has been properly endorsed and that the person claiming delivery is entitled to the goods. Once the master has released the cargo at the disport he should endorse the B/L as ACCOMPLISHED and date/ sign the remark and file the sheet in the accomplished B/L file . Once this ritual is completed, the other two originals automatically become null and void.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In the chemical business B/L states that goods are deliverable to a named consignee OR ORDER. This makes the B/L NEGOTIABLE and it can be endorsed to someone else if they buy the cargo. Endorsing means adding a clause to the B/L and signing it. If the original consignee signs the reverse with no other remark the B/L becomes as OPEN B/L.&nbsp; If the signature is accompanied by a remark \u201cdeliver to XXX\u201d&nbsp; the document becomes STRAIGHT. If the remark says \u201c deliver to XXX or ORDER\u201d then XXX can further endorse it to someone if they wish to resell the cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The receiver usually surrenders one of the three properly endorsed B/L to the disport agent.&nbsp; The master should not discharge cargo till he is sure that the agent at disport is in possession of the original B/L to avoid cargo getting into unauthorized hands. This is eminently possible as many times chemicals/ veg oils are discharged into barges who in turn is transferring into another couple of barges \u2013commingling and adulterating right under your nose.. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Before the vessel arrives at the discharge , the Bill of Lading may be traded several times which may complicate the identification of the proper receiver.&nbsp; Hence it is&nbsp; important that an original Bill of Lading be handed to the Master with an uninterrupted sequence of endorsements.&nbsp; Likewise, the Bill of Lading must contain a clause stating that the whole cargo may be released against one original Bill of Lading although more than one original exists.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If one of the original bills of ladings out of 3 is placed on board, the charterers must be advised. The remaining 2 originals must have the following P&amp;I recommended words inserted \u201c one original retained on board against which delivery of cargo may be properly made on instructions received from Shipper/ Charterer\u201d. The master should identify the party accordingly.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Master must not accept original B/L for carriage on ship if the shipper or his representative refuses the sign the \u201cReceipt for B/L carried on board\u201d.\u2014he should hand over the B/L only to the consignee named in the receipt.&nbsp; He must not accept original B/L for carriage on board also if the consignee and destination is not named on B/L<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is common practice that three original Bills of Lading are issued, in case one should get dropped by the pigeon. Banks always require original documents to release a payment under a letter of credit, which often takes time, whereas the shipper also has to make sure that an original B/L is present at the port of destination in time to release the cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">When lightering inform parties concerned. Now Master becomes Shipper and is entitled to a Mates receipt from the barge. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Master should always on arrival at the load port, ask the agent to provide a copy of the Bill of Lading form intended to be used&nbsp; and check if it meets his requirements. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">As no ullage can be taken due to the foam on top of the Molasses or turbulent vegetable oils , the &nbsp;quantity can only be calculated by draft survey, and this figure is should be used as Bill of Lading figure.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When discharging cargo against presentation of an original Bill of Lading, the original Bill of Lading must be presented to the Master prior commencement of the discharge operation.&nbsp; If the receiver is identical to the party named as consig\u00adnee in the Bill of Lading the receiver must be able to identify himself upon showing the Bill of Lading, and then the cargo can be released.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the holder of the Bill of Lading is different from the one named as consignee on the Bill of Lading, the Bill of Lading must be duly endorsed to the \u2018new\u2019 receiver, who&nbsp; must be able to show his identity.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If the Bill of Lading is issued \u2018to order\u2019 the holder of the Bill of Lading is the legitimate receiver of the cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Upon presentation of the original Bill of Lading the receiver must always endorse the Bill of Lading as receipt for the cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Master must sign the Bill of Lading and write the date when the voyage was accomplished.&nbsp; i.e. Voyage&nbsp; completed xx date. With the presentation of B/L and the discharge of cargo the voyage is said to be accomplished for ship owners<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; When discharging against L.O.I. a written cargo receipt must always be obtained from the receiver.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When discharging in a port other than the one stated in the Bill of Lading the above guidelines still apply except one major difference, namely that all the original Bills of Lading in circulation must be presented prior to commencement of discharge operation.&nbsp; By doing this the Owners ensure that no other holder of an original Bill of Lading in good faith will request delivery of the cargo in the port stated in the Bill of Lading.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in; text-indent: -63.8pt;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When the vessel is out on time-charter the Master is NEVER to sign Bills of Lading to any destination, which is not within the trading limits advised by Operator.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In addition to the Bill of Lading, there are many other documents which record the quantity and condition of the cargo. The Mate's receipt, cargo manifest, stowage plans, tallies and draft surveys, as well as notebooks, correspondence and reports are all of great evidential value. The carrier will rely on such documents to demonstrate the condition and quantity of the cargo at the time it was entrusted to the Master to defend any claim for loss or damage.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: 12.0pt; margin-left: 20.0pt; margin-right: 20.45pt; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remember there is no legal obligation upon the shipowner to deliver cargo without production of the relevant bills of lading and the P&amp;I rules specifically state that the member (owner) is not entitled to make any recovery from the Association if the cargo is delivered without production of original Bills of Lading. In simple terms, if the cargo is delivered without the original accomplished bill of lading being presented or cargo delivered on production of fraudulent bills, then the cargo has, in effect, been stolen and can leave the owner exposed to an enormous loss. The Master must take great care in examining Bills of Lading. If in any doubt he shall contact the Office immediately and before release of cargo.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-right: 10.6pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; tab-stops: 111.0pt; text-autospace: none;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; letter-spacing: 0.1pt; line-height: 150%;\">B</span><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">/Ls<span style=\"letter-spacing: -0.15pt;\"> </span>wh<span , serif;\"><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\">When Gandhi met with the British viceroy in 1930 after the salt satyagraha</span></span><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\">, Gandhi took some duty-free salt from his shawl and said, with a smile, that the salt was \"to remind us of the famous Boston Tea Party.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-67\"><a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Tea_Party#cite_note-67\"></a></sup></span> </span></span><br />\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Now what is the Boston tea party?--pray?</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ2YQmG0nxI/AAAAAAAACFQ/njOh3Ys9x4o/s1600/images+%252811%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ2YQmG0nxI/AAAAAAAACFQ/njOh3Ys9x4o/s1600/images+%252811%2529.jpg\" /></span></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">How did it trigger the American war of Independence? </span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">This is the official version!</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">The British East India Company had controlled all tea trading between India and the British colonies. As a result of the tea tax, the colonies refused to buy the British tea. Instead, they smuggled tea in from Holland. This left the British East India Company with warehouses full of unsold tea, and the company was in danger of going out of business.</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><i><span style=\"color: black;\">The British government was determined to prevent the British East India Company from going out of business. It was going to force the colonists to buy their tea. In May 1773, Prime Minister North and the British parliament passed the Tea Act. The Tea Act allowed the British East India Company to sell tea directly to the colonists, bypassing the colonial wholesale merchants. This allowed the company to sell their tea cheaper than the colonial merchants who were selling smuggled tea from Holland.</span></i><i></i></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">This act revived the colonial issue of taxation without representation. The colonies once again demanded that the British government remove the tax on tea. In addition, the dockworkers began refusing to unload the tea from ships.</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">The Governor of Massachusetts demanded that the tea be unloaded. He also demanded that the people pay the taxes and duty on tea.</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; mso-margin-bottom-alt: auto; mso-margin-top-alt: auto;\">\n<i><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></i></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><i><span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><span style=\"color: red; font-size: large;\"><b>On the evening of December 16, 1773</b></span>, a group of men calling themselves the \"Sons of Liberty\" went to the Boston Harbor. The men were dressed as Mohawk Indians. They boarded three British ships, the Beaver, the Eleanor and the Dartmouth, and dumped forty-five tons of tea into the Boston Harbor.</span></i></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">What actually happened?</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ2YdtKUyRI/AAAAAAAACFU/z2haN4fyY70/s1600/images+%252810%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ2YdtKUyRI/AAAAAAAACFU/z2haN4fyY70/s1600/images+%252810%2529.jpg\" /></span></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\">A group of &nbsp;25 men ( NOT 150 as per propaganda ) , WITH FACES PAINTED BLACK -- all of them thinly disguised as Mohawk Indians</span><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: #0645ad;\">&nbsp;( just to give them a licence to carry an axe )&nbsp;</span></span><span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\">, boarded the three vessels and, over the course of three hours, <span style=\"color: red; font-size: x-large;\">broke each and every chest</span> and dumped all 342 chests of tea into the water. </span></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n<span style=\"color: red; font-size: large;\">When you make symbolic protests , there is NO dire need to break 100% chests, right? --unless you are stupid--</span><br />\n</span></span><br />\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><span style=\"color: red; font-size: large;\"><br /></span></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ3KZmUVUxI/AAAAAAAACFg/JKx3kC-Lc8A/s1600/images+%25289%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ3KZmUVUxI/AAAAAAAACFg/JKx3kC-Lc8A/s1600/images+%25289%2529.jpg\" /></span></a></div>\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">THE KEY THING IS ALL OF THEM , ( SENT BY DRUG RUNNERS ) , CARRIED HATCHETS MEANT FOR BREAKING OPEN EVERY CHEST OF TEA AND SIFTING FOR HIDDEN SATCHELS OF OPIUM INSIDE . &nbsp;AND THEY TOOK ONLY THE OPIUM AWAY &nbsp;\u2014 REST OF THE 90000 POUNDS OF TEA WAS DUMPED INTO THE WATER. &nbsp;&nbsp;</span></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">THE OPIUM SATCHELS CONTAINED MANY TIMES MORE VALUE FOR MONEY-- THAN SIMPLE TEA.</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">FROM 1773 TO 1834, THE POWERFUL AND DEADLY OPIUM IMPORTERS ( WE ALL KNOW THIS POWERFUL SECRET SOCIETY OF USA , STILL CONTROLLING SWISS MONEY ) UNDER PAIN OF DEATH, PREVENTED ALL NEWSPAPERS FROM PUTTING THIS EVENT TO PRINT. &nbsp;</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; color: red; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><b><u>I DARE ANYBODY TO SHOW SOME NEWS ABOUT THE \" BOSTON TEA PARTY FROM 1773 TO 1834.&nbsp;&nbsp;</u></b></span></span><br />\n<span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><br />\n</span><br />\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow; color: red; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"><b><u>&nbsp;I must say that this \"trigger\" for War of Independence , had a amazingly long fuse.</u></b></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"> </span></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Almost all the rich southerner slave owners were addicts of Opium. &nbsp;Even Abraham Lincolns wife Mary Todd was addicted to Laudanum ( Opium medicine )</span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\"> </span></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: &quot;times&quot; , &quot;times new roman&quot; , serif;\">Only a conscience stricken &nbsp;George Robert Twelves Hewes, ( born in Boston in 1742 ) revealed this in his biography, just before he died\u2014 &nbsp;but he left out the true reason . &nbsp;He did NOT write about opium for fear of retribution to his descendants. &nbsp;He was one of the participants of the \"tea party\" at the age of 31.</span></span><br />\n<span class=\"apple-style-span\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;times&quot; , serif;\"> </span></span></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TQ3MqVHoypI/AAAAAAAACFw/wXcb_twcgIs/s1600/download+%25285%2529.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; It is better to get the unloading temperature and the viscosity of Tall oil at that temperature declared in writing in a proper signed and sealed document . <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"color: red;\">Ideally the viscocity in mPas at 20 deg C should be declared in the B/ lading \u2014as this figure varies GREATLY depending on the solution percentage of rosins , fatty oils , sterols, alcohols etc (or is deliberately fudged).</span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Tall oil is an oxidising , drying oil. Oxidation occurs in 3 phases, liquid, gum and solid.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Tall oil is a spent black liquid from the pulping process whose composition and properties can vary vastly making it imperative to get specs from shippers prior loading or planning stow. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">It could be crude tall oil, distilled tall oil, tall oil fatty acid ( liquid rosin, talleol, tallol )----. It is usually used as paint base .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">On completion of washing fresh water rinse and strip.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; Give a short FW rinse . SS tank can be refreshed with weak Metalbrite if next cargo is sensitive.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 9.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Then wash at 40C short drops one hour each 6 drops. \u2013again rinse with FW<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 9.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; mso-pagination: none; text-autospace: none;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Toluene steam cargo lines or you will have to flush the lines for too long. Further cleaning after caustic can be done if required by Myrcene, Coaltar cleaner, <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">TALL OIL FATTY ACID \u2013is NOT a drying oil like tall oil.&nbsp; It is a yellow oily liquid with acrid adour. Used as cutting oils, soap, emulsifier, lubricants etc. very difficult to clean.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">FOSFA\u2014 Banned <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">MP/ 1C\u2014viscosity varies with heating<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%;
