margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">SG/ 0.9<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Crude tall oil pitch is a semi-drying oil.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: 0.25in; margin-right: 0.25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><b style=\"background-color: yellow;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: large;\">BEFORE HANDLING TALL OIL--YOU MUST UNDERSTAND WHAT IS VISCOSITY</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\">VISCOSITY<o:p></o:p></b></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><br />\n</b></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The viscocity of a chemical cargo determines how easy it is to pump out the product and the amount of residue that will be left after discharge .<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">There are time charterers who will put your ship off hire when you can\u2019t use your deep well centrifugal pump to discharge viscous cargoes which need a screw pump. After 1.1.07 with Cat Y/Z Marpol categories pre-wash depends on viscosity of cargo at DISCHARGE PORT temperature&nbsp; --it becomes all the more imperative to know this branch of Physics\u2014how increase in temperature reduces viscosity.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"background-attachment: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: yellow; background-image: initial; background-origin: initial; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">High-Viscosity Substance means a noxious liquid substance in Category X or Y with a viscosity equal to or greater than 50 mPa.s at the<b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"> unloading</b> temperature.</span></i><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></i></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><i style=\"mso-bidi-font-style: normal;\"><span style=\"background-attachment: initial; background-clip: initial; background-color: yellow; background-image: initial; background-origin: initial; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></i></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">High viscosity chemical should be PRE-washed with hot water, with cold interface removed, and the washing discharged to shore reception facilities..<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Viscosity is internal resistance of a fluid to flow or a measure of fluid friction---thus water is thin having low viscocity and honey is thick having high viscocity.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In a laymans language it is a measure of the ability of a liquid to flow through a hole. (For the highest common denominator-- The force per unit area needed to shear a fluid is proportional to the velocity gradient. This constant of proportionality is the viscosity.)<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">This resistance acts against the motion of any solid object through the fluid and also against motion of the fluid itself past stationary obstacles. Viscosity also acts internally on the fluid between slower and faster moving adjacent layers.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoBodyText\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">All fluids, exhibit viscosity to some degree. Viscosity may be thought of as fluid friction. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Viscosity diminishes as temperature rises, often by about 2% per degree C. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The <em><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\">Poiseuille</span></em> and the <em><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\">Poise</span></em> are units of <em><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\">dynamic viscosity</span></b></em> sometimes called <em><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\">absolute viscosity.&nbsp;</span></em><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">1 Poiseuille (Pl) = 10 poise (P) = 1000 cP<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Phonetically it is spelled <em><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\">pwaz. &nbsp;</span></em></span><i><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Poise</span></i><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"> (P) named after Jean Loius Marie Poisueuille. It is more commonly expressed, particularly in ASTM&nbsp;standards, as <i>centipoise</i> (cP). The centipoise is commonly used because water has a viscosity of 1.0020 cP (at 20 \u00b0C)&nbsp; 1 poise = 100 centipoise = 1 g/( cm.s) = 0.1 Pa\u00b7s.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">1 centipoise = 1 mPa\u00b7s.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Screw pumps can handle 1 million mPas or cP.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The \"thicker\" the fluid, the greater its resistance to shear stress and the more rapid the decay of its flow.<o:p></o:p></span></div><h4 style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><a href=\"http://www.blogger.com/post-edit.g?blogID=3564735312144269387&amp;postID=6580782111448537122\" name=\"Kinematic_viscosity\"></a><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Kinematic viscosity<o:p></o:p></span></h4><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The SI physical unit of kinematic viscosity is the (m<sup>2</sup>/s). The CGS physical unit for kinematic viscosity is the <i><a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stokes_(unit)\" title=\"Stokes (unit)\"><span style=\"color: black;\">stokes</span></a></i> (abbreviated S or St), named after <a href=\"http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Gabriel_Stokes\" title=\"George Gabriel Stokes\"><span style=\"color: black;\">George Gabriel Stokes</span></a> . It is sometimes expressed in terms of <i>centistokes</i> (cS or cSt). <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">1 stokes = 100 centistokes = 1 cm<sup>2</sup>/s = 0.0001 m<sup>2</sup>/s.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Viscosity can be a major factor that affects the value of the <b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\">Reynolds number</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Reynolds number is the ratio of inertial forces to viscous (drag) forces&nbsp; and is used for determining whether a flow will be laminar or turbulent. Laminar flow&nbsp;<span style=\"color: black;\">occurs at low Reynolds numbers, where viscous forces are dominant, and is characterized by smooth, constant fluid motion, while turbulent,&nbsp;on t</span>he other hand, occurs at high Reynolds numbers and is dominated by inertial forces, producing random eddies, vortices and other flow fluctuations.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">The transition between laminar and turbulent flow is often indicated by a critical Reynolds number. Within circular pipes the critical Reynolds number is generally accepted to be 2300<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">If we want to calculate the Reynolds number , we can use the following equation.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">R = 3160 x Q x Gt D x \u00b5</span></b><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"color: black; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">where: R = Reynolds number <br />\nQ = liquid's</span><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"> flow rate, gpm <br />\nGt = liquid's specific gravity <br />\nD = inside pipe diameter, in.<br />\n\u00b5 = liquid's viscosity, cp<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Critical velocity= Visc coefficient X &nbsp;RN/ SG &nbsp;X &nbsp;dia<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">When the Reynolds number is less than 2000, flow will be described as laminar <br />\nWhen the Reynolds number is greater than 4000, flow will be described as turbulent <br />\nWhen the Reynolds number is in the range of 2000 to 4000 the flow is considered transitional. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">For e.g You may find highly viscous hydraulic oils may exhibit laminar flow in <span style=\"color: black;\">most conditions while things like water will be turbulent<o:p></o:p></span></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"color: black;\"><br />\n</span></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">NOW LET US DIGRESS BACK TO CHEMISTRY <o:p></o:p></span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></b></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">High Viscosity Substance</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">A substance meets the criteria of a high viscosity substance, if the viscosity exceeds a certain limit, that depends on the Product Group.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In the old system ( before 31<sup>st</sup> Dec 2006 )</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"> if a product was in Category A or B, or Category C and within a special area and the viscosity at discharge conditions is greater than or equal to 25 mPa*s, the substance has to be treated as high viscosity substance. &nbsp;If the product is Category C and outside of a special area and the viscosity at discharge conditions is greater than or equal to 60 mPa*s, the substance has to be treated as high viscosity substance. <o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"background-color: yellow; font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">In the new system after 1<sup>st</sup> Jan 2007&nbsp; </span></b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"background-color: yellow;\">a high-Viscosity Substance means a noxious liquid substance in Category X or Y with a <b><span style=\"color: red;\">viscosity equal to or greater than 50 mPa.s at the unloading temperature.</span></b></span><span style=\"color: red;\"> </span><o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><b style=\"mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;\"><span style=\"color: red;\"><br />\n</span></b></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Products with a high viscosity</span></b><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">These products should be washed at higher temperatures. In general the <span style=\"color: black;\"><a href=\"http://localhost/index.vis?act_id=4\" target=\"_parent\"><span style=\"color: black;\">viscosity</span></a></span> is closely related to the temperature and will decrease at&nbsp;higher temperatures.&nbsp;During washing there should be no ballast water or cold cargoes adjacent to the tank to be cleaned. Washing as soon as possible after discharge is recommended. The respective product characteristic of the individual product must be observed.&nbsp;<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Cargoes with&nbsp; high viscosity require a higher temperature wash water. The wash water then has to be heated to bring the viscocity of the chemical down. Remember the HO bunkers taken by chief engineer is reduced in viscocity from 380 cst to 15 cst prior to injection into the ME\u2014the heating to be done, say upto 135 deg C is known to him.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"TxBrp3\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br />\n</span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">Some chemicals like LO additives, veg/ animal oils, polyols etc do not have a defined MP, but a range. For such cargoes viscocity is used as a measurement of the products liquidity of handling characteristics, and the term pour point is used instead.<o:p></o:p></span></div><div style=\"line-height: 150%; text-align: justify;\"><br />\n</div><div style=\"text-align: justify;\"><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TRYXQzGYBxI/AAAAAAAACYw/6Y9dOXNNPq8/s1600/ab+JERRY+.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"254\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_tugjD0mUn6M/TRYXQzGYBxI/AAAAAAAACYw/6Y9dOXNNPq8/s320/ab+JERRY+.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif;\"><span class=\"Apple-style-span\" style=\"font-size: 15px; line-height: 22px;\"><br />\n</span></span></div></div><div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\"></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><br />\n</div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL ( 28 years in command )<o:p></o:p></span></div><div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin-bottom: .0001pt; margin-bottom: 0in; margin-left: .25in; margin-right: .25in; margin-top: 0in;\"><span style=\"font-family: Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 11pt; line-height: 150%;\">..<o:p></o:p></span></div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt.
